VIDEO GAMES IN THE 20TH CENTURY







  • 1951
    • ☆

    The first computer game. NIMROD, created in 1951.
    This was an evolution of the game presented at
    the Worlds Fair.






  • 1952
    • ☆

    OXO or Noughts and Crosses is a video game developed
    by A S Douglas in 1952 which simulates a game
    of noughts and crosses. It was one of the first
    games developed in the early history of
    video games.






  • 1972
    • ☆

    Atari was created by Nolan Bushnell and Ted Dabney in
    1972 and became a pioneer in arcade games, home
    video game consoles and home computers.






  • 1973
    • ☆

    Empire, which was played over the PLATO network,
    offers the first time a game could be played
    on multiple screens. This creates the
    first time-sharing consoles.






  • 1974
    • ☆

    Dungeons & Dragons is a fantasy tabletop role-playing
    game originally designed by Gary Gygax and Dave
    Arneson. It was first published in 1974. D&D's
    publication is commonly recognized as the
    beginning of modern role-playing
    games and the role-playing
    game industry.






  • 1974
    • ☆

    Spasim is released, which is a 3D shooter game
    that had the ability to connect 32 consoles.
    The stage is beginning to be set for
    multiplayer games.






  • 1975
    • ☆

    In 1975 we have the joystick hit arcade games,
    the first example of a multiplayer human-
    to-human combat shooter. It was a big
    deal when it first hit arcades. It came
    with a new style of gameplay, using
    one joystick to control movement and
    another for shooting direction that
    had never been seen before.






  • 1980
    • ☆

    Space Invaders is a 1978 arcade game created
    by Tomohiro Nishikado. It was the first fixed
    shooter. Space Invaders is considered one
    of the most influential video games of
    all time. It helped expand the video game
    industry from a novelty to the global
    industry and ushered in the golden
    age of arcade video games.






  • 1984
    • ☆

    In 1984, BITNET develops MAD. This is the first
    game to be accessed by a world-wide
    computer network.






  • 1986
    • ☆

    SGI Dogfight, which becomes the first game to
    use the Internet Protocol (TCP/IP), is released
    in 1986. The game was limited to a single
    network, as broadcast packets
    were used.






  • 1987
    • ☆

    In 1987, Atari joins the multiplayer party. With
    the release of Midi Maze, the Atari ST allows
    you to connect up to 16 consoles. This
    is the first time we see the concept
    of a “death match” in gaming.






  • 1993
    • ☆

    Doom is a 1993 first-person shooter video game
    by id Software for MS-DOS. It is considered
    one of the most significant and influential
    titles in video game history, for having
    helped to pioneer, along with the
    1992 Wolfenstein 3D, the now-
    ubiquitous FPS gameplay type.






  • 1995
    • ☆

    Nintendo makes an attempt in Japan for online
    multiplayer support in 1995. They released
    the Satellaview for Super Famicom, but
    this was only available in Japan.






  • 1996
    • ☆

    Quake was the first multiplayer first-person
    shooter game. developed by id Software
    and published by GT Interactive in 1996.
    Owing to its popularity, it would
    become the first game in the
    Quake series.






  • 1997
    • ☆

    Ultima Online is a massively multiplayer online
    role-playing game (MMORPG), released on
    September 24, 1997, by Origin Systems.
    It is a fantasy role-playing game set
    in the Ultima universe. It is known
    for its extensive player versus
    player combat system.






  • 1998
    • ☆

    StarCraft is a military science fiction real-time strategy
    video game developed and published by Blizzard
    Entertainment and released for Microsoft
    Windows computers on March 31,1998. The
    game spawned a franchise and
    became the first game of
    the StarCraft series.






  • 1998
    • ☆

    Lineage is a medieval fantasy, massively
    multiplayer online role-playing game
    released in the United States in 1998 by
    the South Korean computer game
    developer NCsoft. It is the first
    game in the Lineage series. The game
    utilizes an isometric camera view
    and places a strong emphasis
    on PvP combat.
